The Objection and First Refutation
Objection and initial refutation on cause/nature's effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that a contingent being could be pre-eternal because of a pre-eternal cause or nature, and Sanusi's initial refutation that cause and nature have no effect in originated things.

Core Idea
An eternal cause cannot make a contingent effect eternal.

Sanusi anticipates a clever objection: perhaps a contingent being could be pre-eternal if it has a pre-eternal cause or nature. He responds with a foundational principle already proven elsewhere: cause and nature have absolutely no effect in originated things. This lesson walks through the objection and that key refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage. The objector claims that a contingent being might be pre-eternal due to a pre-eternal cause or nature, so contingency does not necessitate origination.
The objector is trying to separate contingency from temporal origination.
2
Understand Sanusi's first refutation
Read the refutation: Sanusi says it has been proven that cause and nature have no effect in any originated thing. This is a sweeping dismissal of the objection's basis.
He refers to a previous proof; we accept it as a given in this context.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why does this refutation work? If cause and nature are ineffective, then even if something has an eternal cause, that cause cannot make it eternal.
This argument underscores the absolute contingency and origination of everything besides Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : لعله جائز الوجودِ مِنْ حيث ذاته ، وقديم لقدم عليه أو طبيعتِه ، فلم يلزم من جوازه حدوثه
قلنا : قد سبق بالبرهان أنَّ العلَّةَ والطبيعةَ لا أثر لهما ألبتة في شيء مِنَ الكائناتِ ، ولهذا أعرضنا في الأصل عن هذا السؤال وجوابه . وأيضاً : فتقديرُ عدمِ القديم مع وجودِ علَّتِهِ أو طبيعتِهِ محالٌ؛ لِمَا يلزم عليهِ مِنْ نفي المسبَّبِ معَ وجودِ السببِ، فإِنْ قُدْرَ أَنَّ سببَهَ انتفى أيضاً نقلنا الكلام إلى نفيه وتسلسل ، وإنْ قُدْرَ أنَّ النفي مع وجودِ الطبيعة لطريانِ ضدٍّ.. كانَ مُحالاً؛ لأنَّ الضدَّ إِنْ طراً قبل عدم القديم لزم اجتماع الضدَّينِ، وإن طراً بعد عدمِهِ لزم عدم القديم لا لسبب . وأيضاً : ففيه ترجيح المرجوح؛ إذ منعُ القديم السابق وجوده لتجدُّدِ هذا الضدِّ أُولى مِنْ منع الضدِّ الطارئ لوجود القديم فخرج بهذا البرهان صدقُ الصغرى
If you say: Perhaps it is contingent in its essence, and pre-eternal due to a pre-eternal cause or its nature, so its contingency does not necessitate its origination.
We say: It has already been proven by demonstration that the cause and nature have absolutely no effect in any of the originated things, and for this reason we refrained in the main discussion from this question and its answer. Also: The assumption of non-existence of the pre-eternal while its cause or nature exists is impossible, because of the necessary consequence of negating the effect while the cause exists. If it is assumed that its cause also ceased to exist, we transfer the discussion to its negation and [thus] an infinite regress. And if it is assumed that the negation [occurs] while the nature exists due to the occurrence of a contrary, it is impossible; because if the contrary occurs before the non-existence of the pre-eternal, the co-existence of two contraries would be necessary, and if it occurs after its non-existence, the non-existence of the pre-eternal would occur without a cause. Also: In it there is a preference of the weaker [alternative]; for preventing the pre-eternal whose existence is prior due to the renewal of this contrary is more appropriate than preventing the emerging contrary for the sake of the existence of the pre-eternal. Thus, by this proof the truth of the minor premise is established.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical objection and its refutation. The objection claims that a contingent being could be pre-eternal if it has a pre-eternal cause or nature. The refutation proceeds in three stages: (1) Cause and nature have no effect in originated things (already proven elsewhere). (2) Assuming non-existence of the pre-eternal while its cause exists is absurd; if the cause also ceases, infinite regress; if a contrary prevents the effect, contradictions arise. (3) There is an unwarranted preference of the weaker alternative. The conclusion is that the minor premise is true.

Key Terms

قديم
علة
طبيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A contingent thing can be eternal if it has an eternal cause or nature.
Correction: Sanusi argues that causes and natures have no effect on originated things, so an eternal cause cannot make a contingent effect eternal.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's first refutation, why does the objection fail?
A) Because the cause is not truly eternal
B) Because cause and nature have no effect in originated things
C) Because the contingent being's essence prevents pre-eternality
D) Because the objection leads to infinite regress

Key Takeaway
Cause and nature have no effect in originated things, so an eternal cause cannot make a contingent being pre-eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you rely most on created causes (effort, people, circumstances) as if they have true effect, and how does this passage challenge you to recenter your trust in Allah alone?
?
The objector tried to escape the implication of contingency by appealing to an eternal cause. When you face accountability for your actions, do you subtly excuse yourself by pointing to external factors? What would it mean to fully accept that cause has no effect and that you stand directly before Allah?

Impossibility and Preference Arguments
Further refutations: impossibility under cause and preference argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional refutations Sanusi provides: the impossibility of a contingent being's non-existence while its cause exists, and the argument that the objector's position involves preferring the weaker alternative.

Core Idea
If a contingent being were pre-eternal, its non-existence would be impossible or lead to absurdity.

Sanusi offers two further arguments against the objection. The first shows that assuming the pre-eternal being ceases to exist while its cause exists is impossible, leading to either infinite regress or contradiction. The second argues that preventing the pre-eternal being from existing due to a new contrary is an arbitrary preference. These arguments solidify the truth of the minor premise that the world is originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the passage starting with 'وأيضاً : فتقديرُ'. Sanusi argues that it is impossible for the pre-eternal being to cease to exist while its cause or nature exists, because that would be an effect without a cause.
He then considers two scenarios: the cause also ceases (infinite regress), or a contrary prevents it (contradiction).
2
Understand the third argument
Read the part starting with 'وأيضاً : ففيه ترجيح المرجوح'. Sanusi says that preventing the pre-eternal from existing to allow a new contrary is an arbitrary preference, since the pre-eternal is prior.
This is a point about fairness in reasoning.
3
See the conclusion
The passage ends with 'فخرج بهذا البرهان صدقُ الصغرى' – thus the minor premise (that the world is originated) is established.
This ties back to the original cosmological argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قلنا : قد سبق بالبرهان أنَّ العلَّةَ والطبيعةَ لا أثر لهما ألبتة في شيء مِنَ الكائناتِ ، ولهذا أعرضنا في الأصل عن هذا السؤال وجوابه . وأيضاً : فتقديرُ عدمِ القديم مع وجودِ علَّتِهِ أو طبيعتِهِ محالٌ؛ لِمَا يلزم عليهِ مِنْ نفي المسبَّبِ معَ وجودِ السببِ، فإِنْ قُدْرَ أَنَّ سببَهَ انتفى أيضاً نقلنا الكلام إلى نفيه وتسلسل ، وإنْ قُدْرَ أنَّ النفي مع وجودِ الطبيعة لطريانِ ضدٍّ.. كانَ مُحالاً؛ لأنَّ الضدَّ إِنْ طراً قبل عدم القديم لزم اجتماع الضدَّينِ، وإن طراً بعد عدمِهِ لزم عدم القديم لا لسبب . وأيضاً : ففيه ترجيح المرجوح؛ إذ منعُ القديم السابق وجوده لتجدُّدِ هذا الضدِّ أُولى مِنْ منع الضدِّ الطارئ لوجود القديم فخرج بهذا البرهان صدقُ الصغرى

Thus, by this proof the truth of the minor premise is established.

?

The First Proof: Inseparability of Bodies from Accidents
Sanusi presents the first proof for the major premise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof for the major premise: that bodies are necessarily inseparable from originated accidents, therefore they themselves are originated.

Core Idea
Bodies cannot exist without originated accidents; so they must be originated too.

Sanusi now proves the major premise of his cosmological argument. He begins by pointing out that bodies are always found with certain accidents like motion, rest, combination, and separation. These accidents are known to be originated, and since bodies are inseparable from them, bodies themselves must be originated. Let's examine this proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
Pay attention to the syllogistic structure.
2
Identify the key components
Look for the major premise, the claim of inseparability, and the specific accidents mentioned.
The classical accidents akwān are motion, rest, combination, separation.
3
Understand the logical structure
The proof is a syllogism: bodies are inseparable from originated accidents; whatever is inseparable from originated accidents is originated; therefore bodies are originated.
This is a concise summary of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دليلُ الكبرى - وهي قولنا : ( وكلُّ مَنْ صفاته حادثةٌ فهو حادث ) - : فهو ما أشرنا إليه في الأصلِ مِن استحالة عروّ الموصوف عن صفاته، وهذهِ الاستحالة معلومةٌ في أكوان العالم بالضرورة؛ لأنَّه لا يمكنُ أنْ يتقرَّرَ في العقلِ جِرمٌ ليس بمتحرك ولا ساكن، ولا مجتمع ولا مفترق، وهي تكفي في الاستدلال بها على حدوثها فتقولُ : العالمُ ملازمٌ ضرورةً للأكوان الحادثة، وكلُّ ملازم للأكوانِ الحادثة فهو حادث؛ فالعالم حادث

وإن شئتَ فاستدل باستحالةِ عرو الأجرام عن الأكوانِ على استحالة عروها عما عداها مِنْ أجناس الأعراض؛ وذلكَ أَنَّ قبول الموصوفِ لجميع صفاتِهِ نفسي لذاتِهِ لا يختلفُ فيها، ولا يطرأ على الذاتِ؛ لئلا يلزم التسلسل في احتياج القبولِ إلى قبول وهلم جراً، فلو جاز العرو عن بعضها لجاز العرو عن جميعها، لكن العرو عن جميعها باطل على الضرورة؛ لِمَا عرفتَ مِن استحالة عروّ الأجرام عن الأكوان، فيلزمُ ألا يجوز عرو الأجرام عن غيرها، وإذا عرفت استحالة عرو الأجرام عن الحوادث.. لزم حدوثها ضرورةً؛ إذ لو كانَتِ الأجرام موجودةً في الأزلِ وصفاتُها لأجل حدوثها لا تُوجَدُ إلا فيما لا يزالُ.. لَلزِمَ عرو الأجرام عن جميع صفاتها، وهو الذي فرغنا قبلُ مِنْ بيانِ استحالتِهِ

هذا بيان ما يتعلَّق بالدليل الذي أشرنا إليه في الأصل

واعلم : أنا أطلقنا فيهِ لفظَ ( العالم ) وأردنا به بعضَه؛ وهو
As for the proof of the major premise—which is our statement: 'And everyone whose attributes are originated is originated'—it is what we indicated in the main discussion from the impossibility of the described [subject] being devoid of its attributes. And this impossibility is known necessarily in the accidents (akwān) of the world; because it is impossible for a body (jirm) to be conceived in the mind as neither moving nor still, nor as neither combining nor separating. This is sufficient for inference to their origination. So you say: The world is necessarily inseparable from the originated accidents, and everything inseparable from originated accidents is originated; therefore the world is originated.

And if you wish, infer from the impossibility of bodies being devoid of accidents (akwān) to the impossibility of their being devoid of other kinds of accidents. This is because the subject's receptivity to all its attributes is intrinsic to its essence—it does not differ in them, and does not occur to the essence [anew], lest an infinite regress result in the need of receptivity for receptivity, and so on. So if being devoid of some were possible, being devoid of all would be possible. But being devoid of all is necessarily false, due to what you know of the impossibility of bodies being devoid of accidents. Hence it follows that it is not permissible for bodies to be devoid of others [i.e., other accidents]. And when you know the impossibility of bodies being devoid of originated things, their origination necessarily follows; because if bodies existed in pre-eternity while their attributes—due to their origination—exist only in the perpetual future, then bodies would be devoid of all their attributes—which we have already finished explaining its impossibility.

This is the exposition of what pertains to the proof we indicated in the main discussion.

And know: We used the term 'world' in it [i.e., the proof], intending by it a part thereof.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the major premise: 'Whatever has originated attributes is itself originated.' The author gives two proofs. First: Bodies are necessarily inseparable from accidents (motion, rest, combination, separation), which are known to be originated. Therefore the world is originated. Second: The impossibility of bodies being devoid of all accidents. Since receptivity to attributes is intrinsic, if it were possible to be devoid of some, it would be possible to be devoid of all. But being devoid of all is impossible, so being devoid of any is impossible. Since all attributes are originated, bodies must be originated. The passage concludes with a note that the term 'world' here refers to a part of the world, i.e., bodies.

Key Terms
دليل الكبرى
استحالة عرو
أكوان
جرم
ملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why must bodies be originated?
A) Because they are created by God
B) Because they are inseparable from originated accidents
C) Because they cannot be imagined
D) Because the world is contingent

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that bodies are necessarily bound to originated accidents, so they themselves must be originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that your own body cannot be conceived without accidents like motion and rest. In what way does this truth challenge the feeling or assumption that you are independent and self-sustaining? How would your day change if you repeatedly reminded yourself that you are constantly 'in need' of a Creator to keep those accidents in existence?
?
Sanusi says the impossibility is known necessarily. Do you have the same level of certainty about the existence of Allah as you do that a body cannot be without motion or rest? If not, what is the specific barrier in your heart or mind? What step can you take today to close that gap?
?
If the world is originated, then it had a beginning and a Beginner. Spend sixty seconds honestly: do you live as if this is true? Where in your daily routine do you act as though the world is self-sufficient or eternal? What would it actually mean for you to live every moment as a created sign of Allah?

The Second Proof: Impossibility of Being Devoid of All Attributes
Sanusi presents the second proof, based on the impossibility of being devoid of all attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof for the major premise: that the impossibility of bodies being devoid of all attributes entails their origination.

Core Idea
If bodies could be without some attributes, they could be without all; but they cannot be without all; so they must have all, which are all originated.

Sanusi offers a second, more general proof. He argues that the subject's receptivity to attributes is intrinsic, so if it were possible for a body to be devoid of some attributes, it would be possible to be devoid of all. But we know from the first proof that bodies cannot be devoid of the primary accidents. Therefore, they cannot be devoid of any attributes. Since all attributes are originated, bodies must be originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the second proof carefully to follow the logical argument.
Notice how it builds on the first proof.
2
Understand the key principle
Grasp that receptivity to attributes is intrinsic and uniform, so if one type is impossible to be devoid of, that applies to all types.
This is the core insight of the proof.
3
See the reduction to impossibility
If bodies could be devoid of some attributes, they could be devoid of all, but the first proof shows being devoid of all is impossible, so bodies are never devoid of any attributes.

Source Text

The First Proof: The World's Inseparability from Accidents
Sanusi presents the first syllogistic proof of the world's temporality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first syllogistic proof for the world's temporal origination based on its inseparability from temporally originated accidents.

Core Idea
The world's inseparability from changing accidents proves its own temporality.

This lesson introduces the foundational kalām argument for the world's creation. Sanusi presents a concise syllogism that moves from observation of accidents to the temporality of the entire world. Let's examine each step carefully to grasp how this simple logical structure carries profound theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Let the syllogistic rhythm sink in.
Notice the structure: premise, second premise, conclusion.
2
Identify the three parts of the syllogism
The passage has a major premise, minor premise, and conclusion. Locate each.
The major premise: 'al-ʿālam mulāzim ḍarūratan li-l-akwān al-ḥāditha'. The minor premise: 'kullu mulāzim li-l-akwān al-ḥāditha fa-huwa ḥādith'. Conclusion: 'fa-l-ʿālam ḥādith'.
3
Understand 'necessary inseparability'
The world is necessarily inseparable from accidents. This is based on observation that accidents always exist in the world and are constantly changing.
This inseparability is a key empirical claim.
4
Reflect on why this proves temporality
Since the accidents are temporally originated (they change), and the world can never exist without them, the world itself must also be temporally originated.
This is a logical rule: if A is inseparable from B and B is temporary, then A is temporary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي تكفي في الاستدلال بها على حدوثها فتقولُ : العالمُ ملازمٌ ضرورةً للأكوان الحادثة ، وكلُّ ملازم للأكوان الحادثة فهو حادث ; فالعالم حادث
And it suffices in inference to its temporal origination, so one says: The world is necessarily inseparable from temporally originated accidents, and whatever is inseparable from temporally originated accidents is itself temporally originated; so the world is temporally originated.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a concise syllogistic proof for the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world. The author states that the world is necessarily inseparable (mulāzim ḍarūratan) from temporally originated accidents (al-akwān al-ḥāditha). Then he applies the general rule: whatever is inseparable from a temporally originated thing is itself temporally originated. The conclusion follows: the world is temporally originated. This is a foundational argument in kalām cosmology, relying on observation of accidents changing.

Key Terms
العالم (al-ʿālam: the world)
الأكوان الحادثة (al-akwān al-ḥāditha: temporally originated accidents)
ملازم (mulāzim: inseparable)
حادث (ḥādith: temporally originated)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular: it assumes what it wants to prove (that the world is temporal) because the accidents are part of the world.
Correction: The argument is not circular because it distinguishes between the world (as substance) and accidents. The temporality of accidents is established independently through direct observation of change. The rule about inseparability then transfers that temporality to the substance.

Checkpoint
In the first proof, what is the relationship between the world and temporally originated accidents?
A) The world is completely free of them.
B) The world is necessarily inseparable from them.
C) The world is accidentally connected to them.
D) The world is the cause of them.

Key Takeaway
The world must be temporally originated because it is inseparable from temporally originated accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi's proof shows that the world is temporally originated. If you truly accept this, how must it change the way you live today? Write a concrete action you will take before the end of this week.
?
The argument relies on the observation that the world is constantly changing. When you look at your own life, what specific change do you see that reminds you of your own temporality? How does that make you feel about your relationship with the Eternal?
?
If you were to reject this proof, what would be the consequence for your belief in God? Can you honestly say you have examined whether you accept it? Commit to a small step to verify the truth of this argument for yourself.

Second Proof: Impossibility of Bodies Being Free from Accidents
Sanusi argues from impossibility of bodies being free from accidents to their temporal origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's second proof for the temporal origination of bodies, based on the impossibility of bodies being free from accidents and the uniformity of receptivity.

Core Idea
If bodies could lack some accidents, they could lack all – but they can't.

Sanusi presents a more intricate proof building on the earlier foundation. He argues that since bodies cannot be free from the accidents of motion and rest, and since the capacity to receive attributes is uniform, bodies cannot be free from any accidents at all. This forces the conclusion that bodies are temporally originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a compressed logical style.
2
Identify the key principle
The passage states that the subject's acceptance of all its attributes is intrinsic (nafsī) and uniform. Find this statement and understand its meaning.
This principle is crucial for the proof.
3
Follow the conditional logic
Trace the argument: if freedom from some accidents were possible, then freedom from all would be possible. But freedom from all is impossible because bodies are never free from akwān.
The impossibility of freedom from akwān is taken as known from earlier.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since bodies cannot be free from any accidents, and accidents are temporally originated, bodies must also be temporally originated.
This is the conclusion of the proof.
5
Check the common misunderstanding
One might think that freedom from some accidents is possible, but the uniform receptivity prevents that. Review the misconception below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شئتَ فاستدل باستحالةِ عرو الأجرام عن الأكوانِ على استحالة عروها عما عداها مِنْ أجناس الأعراض (۱) ; وذلكَ أَنَّ قبول الموصوفِ لجميع صفاتِهِ نفسي لذاتِهِ لا يختلفُ فيها ، ولا يطرأ على الذاتِ ; لئلا يلزم التسلسل في احتياج القبولِ إلى قبول وهلم جراً ، فلو جاز العرو عن بعضها لجازَ العرقُ عن جميعها ، لكن العرو عن جميعها باطل على الضرورة ; لِمَا عرفتَ مِن استحالة عروّ الأجرام عن الأكوان (۲) ، فيلزمُ ألا يجوز عرو الأجرام عن غيرها ، وإذا عرفت استحالة عرو الأجرام عن الحوادث.. لزم حدوثها ضرورةً ; إذ لو كانَتِ الأجرام موجودةً في الأزلِ وصفاتُها لأجل حدوثها لا تُوجَدُ إلا فيما لا يزالُ . . لَلزِمَ عرو الأجرام عن جميع صفاتها ، وهو الذي فرغنا قبلُ مِنْ بيانِ استحالتِهِ
And if you wish, then infer by the impossibility of bodies being free from accidents (akwān) the impossibility of their being free from other [genera] of accidents. That is because the subject's acceptance of all its attributes is intrinsic to its essence, not differing regarding them, nor does it arise upon the essence—lest an infinite regress occur in the need of acceptance for acceptance, and so on. For if freedom from some of them were possible, freedom from all of them would be possible, but freedom from all of them is impossible by necessity, due to what you know of the impossibility of bodies being free from accidents. Thus it follows that it is not permissible for bodies to be free from other [attributes]. And when you know the impossibility of bodies being free from temporally originated things, their temporal origination necessarily follows; for if bodies existed in pre-eternity and their attributes, due to their temporality, exist only in [time]... then freedom of bodies from all their attributes would follow, which we previously finished proving impossible.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a second, more intricate proof of the world's temporality, focusing on bodies (ajrām). The author argues from the impossibility of bodies being free (ʿurū) from accidents (akwān) to the impossibility of their being free from any accident. The reasoning: a subject's capacity to receive all its attributes is intrinsic and uniform; if it could be free from some, it could be free from all. But freedom from all is impossible because bodies are never free from akwān (motion, rest, etc.). Therefore bodies cannot be free from any accident. Since accidents are temporally originated, bodies must also be temporally originated. The proof concludes by noting that if bodies were eternal, they would have to be free from all attributes, which is impossible.

Key Terms
عرو (ʿurū: being free from)
الأجرام (al-ajrām: bodies)
الأكوان (al-akwān: accidents of motion/rest)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul: infinite regress)
نفسي (nafsī: intrinsic)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that bodies can be free from some accidents (e.g., color) while still having others (e.g., motion).
Correction: The argument shows that the subject's capacity to receive attributes is uniform; if it could lack one, it could lack all. Since it cannot lack all (specifically akwān), it cannot lack any.

Checkpoint
What is the key principle in the second proof regarding the subject's acceptance of attributes?
A) It is acquired and varies.
B) It is intrinsic and uniform.
C) It depends on the attribute type.
D) It is impossible to know.

Key Takeaway
Bodies cannot be free from any accidents because their capacity to receive attributes is uniform, and since accidents are originated, bodies must also be originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very existence depends on temporal accidents that are constantly changing, why do you cling to worldly possessions as if they will last forever? What one attachment can you release today to remind yourself you are a created being?
?
The proof shows that bodies cannot be free from attributes because acceptance is intrinsic. In your spiritual life, do you accept that you cannot be free from your nature as a servant of Allah? What is one duty you have been neglecting because you thought you could 'be free' from it?
?
Knowing that you were originated just a moment ago relative to eternity, how does that shape your gratitude? List one blessing you tend to think you 'deserve' but actually have been granted by the Creator out of mercy.

Objection on Attributes and Preliminary Answer
Sanusi clarifies terminology and presents an objection with partial answer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection against the minor premise of the proof for attributes and the initial response based on direct sensory experience.

Core Idea
The objection denies attributes are additional; direct sense perception refutes it.

This passage presents a key objection from those who deny that attributes are distinct from essences. The opponent proposes alternative theories like latency and transfer. Sanusi begins his rebuttal by appealing to what every rational person directly perceives in themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the technical terms like الصغرى and الكمون. Observe how Sanusi first clarifies that 'world' means bodies.
The passage contains footnotes and markers; focus on the main argument.
2
Identify the objection
The objection has two parts: denial that attributes are additional to existence, and denial that they change from non-existence. Find these in the text.
The opponent says: 'لا نسلم أن لذوات العالم صفات زائدة' and then challenges temporality.
3
Understand the opponent's alternatives
The opponent argues attributes are always existent, proposing three mechanisms: latency and manifestation, transfer between loci, or self-subsistence. Note how these avoid change from non-existence.
The text lists these: إما في موصوفها لكن تارة تكمن... إما مع انتقال... أو من قيام بنفسها.
4
Examine the answer
Sanusi begins by refuting the first denial: every rational person senses additional attributes like knowledge and sound. This is direct evidence that attributes are additional to the essence.
The answer is incomplete here but shows the method: appeal to immediate awareness.

This is an explanation of what pertains to the proof we indicated in the original. And know: we used the term 'world' therein and intended by it a part of it—namely the bodies; because he made it described by attributes. And his saying: 'due to the impossibility of its being free from them'—the pronoun in 'its being free' refers to the described, and in 'from them' refers to the attributes. Your saying: 'because they change from non-existence to existence and vice versa' is denied, because we say: they have no non-existence at all; rather they are perpetually existent—either in their described, but sometimes they lie latent in it with the appearance of the judgment of their opposite, and sometimes they appear with the appearance of their judgment, or by transfer from one locus to another, or from self-subsistence to subsistence in a locus, and vice versa. [Establishing accidents, and refuting latent appearance and manifestation, and refuting their transfer, and refuting their self-subsistence] And the answer to the first: that every rational person senses in his essence meanings additional to it, such as knowledge and its opposites, sound and the like. This is why some said...
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage first clarifies that by 'world' the author means bodies, and explains pronoun references. Then it introduces an objection against the minor premise of the proof: the opponent denies that the world's essences have attributes additional to their existence, or that those attributes are temporally originated. The opponent argues that attributes do not change from non-existence but are always existent, either through latency (kumūn) in the subject, manifesting when their opposite recedes, or through transfer (intiqāl) from one subject to another, or by self-subsistence (qiyām bi-nafsihi). The heading indicates that the author will refute these theories. The answer begins by refuting the first denial: every rational person directly perceives additional attributes in themselves, like knowledge and sound, which are distinct from the essence. The answer cuts off mid-sentence, but the refutation of latency and transfer presumably follows.

الكمون (al-kumūn: latent state)
الظهور (al-ẓuhūr: manifestation)
الانتقال (al-intiqāl: transfer)

Misconception: Attributes are not additional to essences; they are always present either as latent or transferred.
Correction: Attributes are perceived as additional and temporally originated; latency and transfer are false theories.

The objection that attributes are not additional is refuted by direct sensory evidence; alternative explanations like latency are to be refuted.

Impossibility of an Infinite Regress of Events
Sanusi proves that postulating an infinite past leads to a contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an infinite regress of temporal events is impossible and how this proof leads to a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
An infinite past would make the present impossible.

This passage presents a crucial argument in Islamic theology: the impossibility of an infinite regress of events. Sanusi demonstrates that postulating an infinite series of past events leads to a contradiction, thereby establishing that the world must have a beginning. Let's follow the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Try to grasp the overall argument without diving into details yet.
Notice that the language is technical but the logic is straightforward.
2
Understand the premise
What does it mean to postulate events with no beginning? This is the hypothesis Sanusi is refuting. Consider what it would entail for the present moment.
The premise is that there is an infinite series of past events, each caused by a previous one.
3
Trace the logical contradiction
Follow how Sanusi shows that an infinite past would require 'completing' an infinite number before the present. Why is that impossible?
Completion of a number requires a first and last term, but an infinite series has no beginning.
4
Identify the conclusion
What is the final conclusion? The assumption leads to present events being impossible, yet they exist. So the assumption is false.
This proves that the series of events must have a beginning.
5
Reflect on the significance
Why is this argument important for Islamic theology? It establishes that the universe is created and not eternal.
This connects to broader discussions about the existence of God and the nature of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلان حوادث لا أول لها وتقديرها حوادث لا مبدأ لها يؤدي إلى فراغ ما لا نهاية له عدداً قبل ما وُجِدَ منها الآنَ ، لكنْ فراغ العددِ يستلزمُ انتهاءَ طرفيهِ ، ففراغ ما لا نهاية لهُ مِنْ عدد الحوادثِ محال ، فما توقَّفَ عليهِ مِنْ وجودِ الحوادثِ الآن يجبُ أنْ يكونَ محالاً ، فيلزم أن تكون عدماً مع تحقق وجودها
The invalidity of events with no beginning: Postulating events with no beginning leads to the completion of an infinite number before what exists now. But the completion of a number necessitates the ending of its two extremities. Therefore, the completion of an infinite number of events is impossible. So what the existence of events now depends upon must be impossible, leading to the necessity that they be nonexistent while their existence is realized.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the impossibility of an infinite regress of temporal events (ḥawādith lā awwal lahā). The argument runs as follows: if there were an infinite number of events with no beginning, then before the events that exist now, an infinite number of events would have already occurred and thus been 'completed.' However, the completion of a number requires that both its endpoints be finite—i.e., it has a first and a last. An infinite number has no endpoint, so its completion is impossible. Therefore, the assumption that the existence of present events depends on an infinite past is impossible. Consequently, if that assumption were true, present events would be nonexistent, but they are manifestly existent. This contradiction shows that the assumption is false, proving that the series of events must have a beginning.

Key Terms
حوادث لا أول لها
فراغ العدد
ما لا نهاية له

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite past is theoretically possible.
Correction: This proof shows that an infinite past leads to a logical contradiction, making it impossible.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does the proof of 'burlān ḥawādith lā awwal lahā' highlight?
A) That an infinite number can be completed
B) That present events would be nonexistent if they depended on an infinite past
C) That everything has a beginning
D) That accidents cannot be transmitted

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of an infinite regress of events proves that the universe must have a beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the universe must have a beginning, then your own existence is contingent on a Cause. Are you living today as if you are self-made, or as a dependent creation? What one habit could you change to acknowledge that dependence?
?
The proof shows that an infinite past is impossible. Your life is a series of finite moments—each with a beginning. Does the way you spend your time reflect an awareness that you are accountable to the One who caused all beginnings?
?
Sanusi’s argument forces you to confront that present events depend on a First Cause. When you woke up this morning, did you consider that your very existence is sustained by that Cause? What would it look like to start your day with that recognition?

The Proof of Cutting and Application (Burhan al-Qat' wa al-Tatbiq)
Sanusi presents the proof of cutting and application to refute infinite temporal events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the proof of cutting and application to demonstrate that an actual infinite series of temporal events is impossible.

Core Idea
An infinite series of events creates a contradiction between countability and comparison.

Sanusi now presents his third and most technical argument against the possibility of an infinite temporal regress. The proof of cutting and application (burhan al-qat' wa al-tatbiq) uses a comparison of two infinite sequences to show that the concept leads to an impossibility. By following his reasoning, you will see why classical theology holds that the universe must have been created at a finite point in time.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof's main claim
Start by reading Sanusi's formal statement of the proof. Notice that it begins with a conditional: if endless events existed, then two numbers would arise that are neither equal nor unequal. This is the central contradiction.
The proof is called 'cutting' because it cuts off the possibility of infinite regress.
2
Understand the example with the Flood and now
Sanusi gives a concrete example: compare the number of events from the Flood to eternity with the number from now to eternity. These are two distinct infinite sets.
Equality is impossible because one set has extra events (between Flood and now).
3
See why inequality is impossible
Since both sets are infinite, neither can be exhausted by counting before the other. Sanusi defines 'smaller' as what is exhausted first, so neither is smaller or larger.
This is the key insight: infinite sets cannot be compared by size in the usual way.
4
Conclude the proof
The only remaining relation between two numbers is equality or inequality. Since neither holds, the situation is impossible. Therefore, the assumption of endless events is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان القطع والتطبيق
وأنْ يستحيل عندَ تطبيق ما فرغ منها بدون زيادة على نفسِهِ معَ زيادةٍ .. ما عُلِمَ بينَ العددينِ مِنْ وجوبِ المساواة أو نقيضها
هذا طريق ثالث لإبطالِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها ، ويُسمَّى هذا البرهان برهان القطع والتطبيق ، وتقريره : أن نقول : لو وُجِدَتْ حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها لَلَزِمَ أَنْ يُوجَدَ عددانِ متغايرانِ ، وليس أحدهما أكثر مِنَ الآخر ولا مساوياً لهُ ! والتالي باطل على الضرورةِ ؛ لما عُلِمَ مِنْ وجوب إحدى النسبتين بين كل عددين ، فيكون ملزومه ـ وهو وجود حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ـ باطلاً .
وبيانُ الملازمة : أنَّا لو نظرنا عدد الحوادثِ مِنَ الطوفانِ مثلاً إلى الأزلِ معَ عددِها مِنَ الآنَ مثلاً إلى الأزلِ . . لكانا عددين متغايرين على الضرورة ، وتستحيل بينهما المساواة ؛ لتحققِ الزيادة في أحدهما ، والشيءُ دونَ زيادةٍ لا يكون مساوياً لنفسِهِ بعد زيادةٍ ، ويستحيلُ أيضاً أنْ يكون أحدهما أكثرَ مِنَ الآخرِ ؛ لعدم تناهي أفراد كل واحدٍ منهما ، فلا يفرغ أحدهما بالعد قبل الآخرِ ، وحقيقة الأقل : ما يصيرُ عندَ العد فانياً قبل الآخرِ ، والأكثر : ما يقابله ، ونحنُ لو فرضنا الآن شخصينِ أحدُهما يَعُدُّ الحوادثَ مِنَ الطوفانِ إلى الأزلِ ، والآخرُ يَعُدُّها مِنَ الآنَ إلى الأزلِ.. لاستحال على مذهبهم أن يفنى أحد العددين بالعد قبل الآخر ! فيمتنع أن أحدهما أكثرُ مِنَ الآخر .
فقد اتضح لكَ : أَنَّهُ يلزمُ على وجودِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها أَنْ يُوجَدَ عددانِ ليس بينهما مساواة ولا مفاضلة
The Proof of Cutting and Application. And that it is impossible, when applying what has been finished from them without increase to itself with increase... that which is known between the two numbers necessitating equality or its opposite. This is a third way to invalidate events that have no beginning, and this proof is called the proof of cutting and application. Its exposition: that we say: if there existed events with no beginning, it would necessarily entail that there exist two distinct numbers, neither of which is greater than the other nor equal to it! And the consequent is necessarily false, because it is known that one of the two relations is necessary between every two numbers. Therefore, its necessary condition — which is the existence of events with no beginning — is false. And the explanation of the entailment: that if we look at the number of events from, for example, the Flood to eternity, together with the number from, for example, now to eternity, they would be two distinct numbers necessarily, and equality between them is impossible due to the actual increase in one of them. And a thing without increase is not equal to itself after increase. It is also impossible that one of them be greater than the other, because each one's individuals are infinite, so one does not finish counting before the other. And the definition of the smaller is: what becomes exhausted in counting before the other, and the greater is its opposite. And if we now suppose two persons, one counting the events from the Flood to eternity, and the other counting them from now to eternity, it would be impossible according to their view for one of the two numbers to be exhausted by counting before the other! Hence it is impossible for one to be greater than the other. Thus it has become clear to you: that the existence of events with no beginning would necessarily require the existence of two numbers between which there is neither equality nor inequality.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents Sanusi's third way to invalidate the claim that there is an infinite regress of temporal events, namely the proof of cutting and application. The passage begins by stating the proof's central claim: that it is impossible, when applying (i.e., comparing) what has been finished from them (the events) without increase to itself with increase, for what is known about the necessity of equality or its opposite between two numbers to hold. He then clarifies that this is a third way to refute endless events and names it the proof of cutting and application. The proof is then given in formal terms: if endless events existed, there would necessarily be two distinct numbers (the count from some past event to eternity and from the present to eternity) that are neither equal nor does one exceed the other—which is absurd given the necessary relation of equality or inequality between any two numbers. Sanusi then explains the entailment by example: consider the number of events from the Flood to eternity and from now to eternity. They are necessarily distinct, equality is impossible because one has more events (from Flood to now), and inequality is impossible because both are infinite so neither is greater. He defines the smaller as that which becomes exhausted first in count, which cannot happen with infinities. He concludes that it is clear that endless events would require two numbers with no equality or inequality, which is impossible; thus the existence of such events is impossible.

Key Terms
برهان القطع والتطبيق
حوادث
أزل
عددان
مساواة
مفاضلة
تطبيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof shows infinity is impossible in any sense.
Correction: The proof specifically shows that an actual infinite series of temporal events is impossible because it leads to a logical contradiction when comparing two such infinite sets. Mathematical abstract infinities are not the subject.

Checkpoint
In the proof of cutting and application, what impossible situation must arise if there were events with no beginning?
A) There would be two numbers that are either equal or one greater than the other.
B) There would be two numbers that are neither equal nor one greater than the other.
C) There would be an infinite number of events.
D) There would be a first event.

Key Takeaway
The proof of cutting and application demonstrates that an actual infinite series of temporal events is logically impossible because it leads to a contradiction between the necessary relations of numbers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the universe had no beginning, as some claim, what would that imply about your own existence and responsibility to a Creator? Do you sincerely grapple with that conclusion?
?
The proof forces you to accept a logical contradiction if you deny a beginning. What parts of your life are you trying to justify as 'unfounded' or 'infinite'—perhaps habits, assumptions, or excuses—that you need to cut and bring to a real start?
?
You have just seen that rational necessity demands a beginning to all temporal things. Will you today let that truth penetrate your heart, or will you continue to live as if there is no accountability beyond this finite life?

The Definition of Pre-Eternity and Its Proof
Sanusi defines qadim and gives the proof for Allah's pre-eternity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of pre-eternity (al-qidam) as applied to Allah and the logical proof that necessitates this attribute for Him.

Core Idea
Pre-eternity means having no beginning; Allah must be pre-eternal or an infinite regress follows.

Sanusi now clarifies the term 'pre-eternity' (al-qidam), distinguishing its true meaning from common usage. He establishes that Allah is described by the attribute of pre-eternity in the sense of having no beginning. Then he begins a crucial proof: if Allah were not pre-eternal, He would be originated, leading to an impossibility. This lesson examines the definition and the first step of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of qadim
Read the definition carefully: qadim is what has no beginning for its existence. Note that Sanusi distinguishes this from other possible meanings of 'old'.
2
See how this meaning applies to Allah
Sanusi states that this second meaning (no beginning) is what is established for Allah. Reflect on why only this meaning is suitable for the Creator.
3
Follow the conditional proof
The proof begins with a conditional: if Allah were not pre-eternal, He would be originated. Think about what follows from that – an infinite chain of causes or a first cause.
The passage cuts off; the conclusion is that Allah must be pre-eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يُطلَقُ القدمُ على : ما لا أوّلَ لوجوده ، أي : وجوده أزلي لم يسبقه عدمٌ ، والقدمُ باعتبار هذا المعنى الثاني هو الثابتُ له جلَّ وعلا . والدليل على وجوبِهِ لهُ جلَّ وعلا : أنَّه لو لم يكن قديماً لكان
And pre-eternity (al-qidam) is sometimes applied to what has no beginning for its existence, i.e., its existence is pre-eternal (azali), no non-existence preceded it. And pre-eternity according to this second meaning is what is established for Him, may He be exalted and magnified. And the proof for its necessity for Him, may He be exalted and magnified, is that if He were not pre-eternal, He would be
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a definition and a proof. After concluding the previous discussion on time, Sanusi turns to clarify the term 'pre-eternity' (al-qidam). He states that 'qadim' is sometimes applied to that which has no beginning for its existence, meaning its existence is pre-eternal (azali) with no non-existence preceding it. This second meaning of al-qidam (pre-eternity) is what is positively affirmed of Allah (may He be exalted). Then he begins the proof that this attribute is necessary for Allah: if He were not pre-eternal (i.e., if He had a beginning), then He would be originated. The proof is a conditional syllogism (reductio ad absurdum): if Allah were not qadim, He would be hadith (originated). Since originated beings require a creator, and that would lead to infinite regress or a first cause, the only logically sound conclusion is that Allah is qadim. The text cuts off with the protasis; the apodosis and conclusion would follow on the next page. The key point is that pre-eternity (having no beginning) is a necessary attribute of Allah, and the proof relies on the impossibility of an infinite regress of originated things.

أزلي
حادث
وجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'qadim' (pre-eternal) means extremely old or existing for a long time.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies it strictly means having no beginning at all, not merely being ancient.

Checkpoint

B) That which has no beginning for its existence.
C) That which is not subject to change.
D) That which is beyond time.

Key Takeaway
Pre-eternity (qidam) is an essential attribute of Allah, meaning His existence has no beginning; the proof for this is based on the impossibility of an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are an originated being—your existence had a beginning. Allah alone has no beginning. Does your daily life reflect this stark dependence, or do you unconsciously act as if you are self-sufficient? This week, pause before each meal and say, 'Alhamdulillah' with the awareness that every blessing comes from the Pre-Eternal One.
?
The proof shows that if Allah were not pre-eternal, an impossible infinite regress would follow. Your own existence is evidence that there must be a First Cause. Have you truly let that fact sink into your heart? When you feel anxiety about the future, remember that your Creator has no beginning and no end—He holds all time. Will you entrust your worries to Him today?
?
If Allah were not pre-eternal, He would be like you—originated. But He is not. How does that difference affect your worship? Do you pray to Him as the One who has always been there, even before you were born? Make a sincere dua today, addressing Him as 'Ya Qadim' (O Pre-Eternal), and ask Him to grant you gratitude for His eternal care.

The Rational Proof for God's Eternity
Sanusi defines qidam (eternity) as having no beginning and provides a proof, then answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for God's eternity (qidam) based on the impossibility of circularity and infinite regress, and how Sanusi answers the objection about time.

Core Idea
God's eternity is proven because any alternative leads to impossible circularity or infinite regress.

This lesson presents Sanusi's definition of God's eternity (qidam) and a powerful rational argument that every existent must be either eternal or contingent. Since contingency for God would require an originator, which in turn would lead to either circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul)—both impossible—God must be eternal. The passage also addresses a subtle objection about time, showing that time itself is created and does not imply an infinite past.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping to analyse. Then read the English translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in before you dissect it.
Notice that Sanusi uses very precise logical terms like 'dawr' and 'tasalsul'.
2
Identify the definition of qidam
Find where Sanusi defines qidam as 'that which has no beginning to its existence'. Note that this is the second meaning of qidam, and it is the attribute of God.
3
Follow the proof chain
The proof goes: if not eternal → contingent → needs an originator → that originator would also be contingent → leads either to circularity (if it is the same) or infinite regress (if different) → both impossible → therefore God is eternal.
Sanusi assumes that opponents accept that infinite regress in causes is impossible.
4
Understand the objection and answer
The objection says that positing an eternal being implies infinite past times, which contradicts your own rejection of infinite regress. Sanusi answers by denying the implication: time itself has no existence before the world.
This shows that time is a created entity, not a necessary container for existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يُطلَقُ القدمُ على : ما لا أوّلَ لوجوده ، أي : وجوده أزلي لم يسبقه عدمٌ ، والقدمُ باعتبار هذا المعنى الثاني هو الثابتُ له جلَّ وعلا
·
والدليل على وجوبِهِ لهُ جلَّ وعلا : أنَّه لو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ؛ إذ لا واسطة بينهما في حقٍّ كلّ موجود ، لكن كونه حادثاً محال ؛ لأنَّهُ يُوجِبُ افتقاره إلى محدثِ ، لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوبِ افتقارِ كل حادث إلى محدِثِ ، ثم ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى محدِثِهِ ، فيكونُ حادثاً كالأوَّلِ ، فيفتقرُ أيضاً إلى محدِثٍ ، فإن كانَ محدِثُهُ الأَوَّلَ الذي كانَ أثراً له .. لزم الدورُ ، وإنْ كانَ غيرَهُ لزمَ في الغير ما لزم فيه وتسلسل ، والتسلسل محال ؛ لما عرفت استحالة حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، والخصومُ القائلون بذلك سلَّموا أنَّ التسلسل في الأسباب والمسبباتِ مستحيل .
فإن قيل : إذا قلتُم بقديم لا أوَّلَ لهُ ففيه إثبات أوقاتٍ متعاقبة لا أَوَّلَ لها ؛ لأنَّ الموجودَ لا يُعقَلُ إلا في وقتٍ ، وثبوتُ أوقاتِ لا أَوَّلَ لها ممنوع ؛ لما قرَّرتُم في حوادث لا أوَّلَ لها ، فقد فررتُم مِنَ التسلسل وقعتُم فيه
فالجواب : منعُ الملازمةِ ؛ لما عرفْتَ أنَّ حقيقة الوقتِ والزمان لا وجود لها قبل وجود العالم ، فقوله : ( أنَّ الموجود لا يُعقَلُ إلا في وقت ) باطل .
إيطال الدور والتسلسل ]
وإلى إبطال التسلسل أشرتُ بقولي في العقيدة : ( لما في الأول - أعني : التسلسل - مِنْ فراغ ما لا نهاية له) أعني : وقد مرَّ بيانُ استحالته ، والباء في قوله : ( بالعدد ) بمعنى ( في ) أي : ما لا نهاية له في عددِهِ .
And al-qidam (eternity) is sometimes applied to: that which has no beginning to its existence, i.e., its existence is eternal (azali), preceded by no non-existence. And al-qidam according to this second meaning is that which is established for Him, Glorified and Exalted. And the proof for its necessity for Him, Glorified and Exalted, is: that if He were not eternal then He would be contingent (hadith), because there is no intermediary between them with respect to every existent. But His being contingent is impossible, because it would necessitate His being in need of an originator (muhdith), as you have known from the necessity of every contingent being needing an originator. Then we transfer the argument to its originator, and it would be contingent like the first, so it would also need an originator. If its originator were the first which was its effect, then circularity (ad-dawr) would follow; and if it were other than that, then what applied to it would apply to the other, and infinite regress (at-tasalsul) would follow. And infinite regress is impossible, because you know the impossibility of an infinite chain of contingent events without a beginning. And the opponents who say that have conceded that infinite regress in causes and effects is impossible. If it is said: If you affirm an eternal being with no beginning, then that involves affirming successive times with no beginning, because an existent is not conceivable except in a time, and the establishment of times with no beginning is prohibited due to what you have established regarding contingent events with no beginning. Thus you have fled from infinite regress and fallen into it. The answer: The denial of the implication, because you know that the reality of time has no existence before the existence of the world. So his statement: 'An existent is not conceivable except in a time' is false. [Refutation of circularity and infinite regress] And towards the refutation of infinite regress I pointed in my statement in al-Aqida: 'because in the first—meaning infinite regress—there is an infinite void' meaning: and the explanation of its impossibility has passed, and the letter ba in his saying 'bi'l-ʿadad' is in the sense of 'fi' (in), i.e., infinite in its number.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of God's eternity (qidam), followed by an objection and its answer. It begins by defining qidam as 'that which has no beginning to its existence'—an eternal existence not preceded by non-existence. This second meaning of qidam is attributed to God. The proof proceeds: if God were not eternal (qadim), He would be contingent (hadith), since every existing thing is either eternal or contingent. Contingency is impossible for God because it would require an originator (muhdith). That originator, if itself contingent, would require another, leading to either circularity (dawr) if it is the same, or infinite regress (tasalsul) if it is different. Both are impossible. The author notes that even opponents concede that infinite regress in causes and effects is impossible. Then an objection is raised: positing an eternal being with no beginning implies successive times with no beginning, which you (the mutakallimun) reject for contingent events—so you have merely replaced one infinite regress with another. The answer is simple: time (waqt/zaman) has no existence before the creation of the world, so the claim that every existent must be in a time is false. The passage concludes with a brief note referencing the author's own work, al-Aqida, on refuting circularity and regress, and clarifying a phrase about an infinite void.

Key Terms
القدم (al-qidam: eternity)
الأزل (al-azal: pre-eternity)
الحادث (al-hadith: contingent)
المحدث (al-muhdith: originator)
الدور (ad-dawr: circularity)
التسلسل (at-tasalsul: infinite regress)
إيطال (ibṭāl: refutation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is an eternal container that must exist for anything to exist, so an eternal being implies infinite past times.
Correction: Time is a created entity; it did not exist before the universe. Thus, God's eternity does not require infinite past times; time began with creation.

Checkpoint
In the proof of God's eternity, what does Sanusi say would happen if the first originator were itself contingent?
A) It would be impossible for it to exist.
B) Either circularity or infinite regress would follow.
C) It would be necessary that it is eternal.
D) The argument would stop at that point.

Key Takeaway
God's eternity is rationally necessary because any alternative leads to an impossible infinite regress or circularity, and the objection that eternity implies timeless times is refuted by the createdness of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's eternity means He has no beginning and depends on nothing, then what created things are you relying on as if they were eternal? Will you release your grip on them and anchor your security solely in Him?
?
The proof shows that any alternative to God's eternity leads to absurdity. When doubts about God's nature cross your mind, do you honestly follow them through to their logical conclusions, or do you avoid the discomfort? What would it cost you to live as if the alternative were true?
?
Time is created and had a beginning. Your entire life is a fleeting moment in that created time. In light of God's timeless eternity, what temporal concerns are you giving too much weight? What would it look like to rearrange your priorities based on the reality of an eternal God?

Refuting the Objection of Infinite Times
Sanusi presents and refutes an objection against an eternal creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that an eternal creator implies an infinite regress of times by denying the implication and asserting the createdness of time.

Core Idea
Time itself is a created entity, so the eternal being does not exist within time.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a critical objection against the doctrine of an eternal creator. The objector argues that positing a being without beginning entails a succession of times without beginning, which contradicts the rejection of infinite regress. Sanusi's answer is a masterful denial of the logical implication, reminding us that time is not an absolute container but a created thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objector's statement: 'If you say there is an eternal being without beginning, then this entails successive times without beginning.' Notice the logical structure: a conditional claim with an unwelcome conclusion.
The objector is trying to show inconsistency.
2
Identify the objector's logical move
The objector argues that since every existent must exist in a time, an eternal being would require an infinite series of times. This, they claim, is the same infinite regress you rejected for contingent events.
This is a classic tu quoque argument.
3
Understand Sanusi's reply
Sanusi denies the logical implication (man' al-mulāzama). He does not argue against infinite regress of times directly; instead, he attacks the premise that every existent must be in a time.
His answer is concise: the premise is false.
4
Grasp the reason: time is created
Sanusi explains that time (waqt) and temporal duration (zamān) have no existence before the world. Therefore, the eternal being does not exist 'in time' in any pre-creation sense. The objection's assumption that time is an absolute container is wrong.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: إذا قلتُم بقديم لا أوَّلَ له ففيه إثبات أوقاتٍ متعاقبة لا أَوَّلَ لها؛ لأنَّ الموجودَ لا يُعقَلُ إلا في وقتٍ، وثبوتُ أوقاتِ لا أَوَّلَ لها ممنوع؛ لما قرَّرتُم في حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها، فقد فررتُم مِنَ التسلسل وقعتم فيه. فالجواب: منعُ الملازمةِ؛ لما عرفْتَ أنَّ حقيقة الوقتِ والزمان لا وجود لها قبل وجود العالم، فقوله : ( أنَّ الموجود لا يُعقَلُ إلا في وقت ) باطل .
If it is said: When you say there is an eternal (qadīm) without beginning, then this entails affirming successive times without beginning, because an existent is only conceivable in a time, and affirming times without beginning is prohibited given what you established regarding contingents without beginning. So you fled from infinite regress and fell into it. The answer: denial of the implication; because you know that the reality of time (waqt) and temporal duration (zamān) has no existence before the existence of the world. So his saying 'an existent is only conceivable in a time' is false.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer unit. The objector argues: If you posit an eternal being (qadīm) with no beginning, that entails a succession of times with no beginning, since every existent must exist in some time. But you rejected infinite regress of contingents; so you are inconsistent—you fled infinite regress but fell into it by positing infinite times. Sanusi's answer is a denial of the logical implication (manʿ al-mulāzama). He explains that time (waqt) and temporal duration (zamān) have no existence prior to the creation of the world. Therefore, there is no pre-world time in which the eternal being would exist; rather, time itself is created. Hence the objection's premise that every existent is in a time is false when applied to the eternal being, because before the world there was no time. Thus the contradiction is resolved.

Key Terms
قديم
وقت
زمان
تسلسل
ملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is an absolute container that exists independently, so an eternal being must exist in an infinite sequence of times.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that time is a created entity and did not exist before the world, so the eternal being is not subject to temporal succession.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi answer the objection that an eternal being implies infinite times?
A) He admits infinite times are possible.
B) He denies the implication, stating that time does not exist before the world.
C) He says the eternal being exists outside time.
D) He argues that infinite times are not like infinite contingents.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes the objection by denying the implication that an eternal being requires infinite times, because time itself is a created entity that did not exist before the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's existence before creation, do you instinctively picture Him 'in some time' because that's how you experience existence? How does knowing that time is a created thing change the way you imagine His eternality? Let this lesson strip away the human limitation you have unknowingly placed on your Lord, and commit to worshipping Him as He truly is—beyond time.
?
The objector assumed that every existent must be in a time. Have you ever made similar assumptions about Allah—like thinking He is distant because you measure His responses by your timeline? How does Sanusi's answer free you from being enslaved to time in your relationship with Allah? Will you now trust that His actions are not bound by your clock?

The Impossibility of Circular Reasoning in Proving the Creator's Eternity
Sanusi refutes circularity in proving the Creator's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why circular reasoning (dawr) is logically impossible and how this refutes any argument that the Creator is contingent.

Core Idea
Circular reasoning forces a thing to be prior and posterior to itself—an absurdity.

The commentator Sanusi presents a logical argument to show that circularity (dawr) is impossible. If the proof of the Creator's eternity were circular, it would lead to a thing being both prior and posterior to itself by two ranks. This absurdity demonstrates that the proof of the Creator's pre-eternity is sound and free from circularity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of circularity
Read the passage's opening: circularity means a single thing being prior to itself and posterior to itself. This is the core concept to grasp.
The commentator defines dawr clearly.
2
Follow the logical consequence
If A is the effect of B, and B is also the effect of A, then A must be prior to B (cause precedes effect) and also posterior to B. This forces A to be two ranks prior and two ranks posterior to itself.
The cause must precede its effect, so reciprocity is impossible.
3
Recognize the concomitant relationship
Priority and posteriority are inseparable in circularity: if a thing is prior to itself, it must also be posterior to itself, and vice versa.
4
Apply the conclusion
Because such circularity is absurd, and the proof of the Creator's eternity is clear and free from it, no rational person has ever claimed the Creator is contingent.
This reinforces the soundness of the orthodox proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا إبطالُ الدَّورِ : فإليهِ أشرتُ بقولي في العقيدة : ( وفي الثاني يعني : الدور - مِنْ كونِ الشيء الواحدِ سابقاً على نفسه مسبوقاً بها ) ، أمَّا لزوم سبقيتِهِ على نفسِهِ : فلأنَّ صانعَهُ أثرٌ لَهُ ، فيجبُ أنْ يتقدَّمَ على صانعه ؛ لوجوبِ سبقِ المؤثر على أثرِهِ ، لكنَّهُ هو أيضاً أثر لصانعه فيجب أن يتقدَّمَ صانعُهُ عليهِ لعين ما ذُكِرَ ، فلزمَ أَنْ يتقدَّمَ على نفسِهِ بمرتبتين ؛ لأنَّهُ مُقدَّمٌ على صانعِهِ المقدَّم على نفسه ، والمقدَّم على المقدَّم على الشيء مُقدَّم على ذلكَ الشيء ضرورةً ، ولذلك أيضاً يجب أنْ يتأَخَّرَ عن نفسِهِ بمرتبتين ، وهو الذي عنيتُ بقولي : ( مسبوقاً بها ( ، وذلكَ لأنَّهُ أثر لصانعِهِ ، فيتأخَرُ عنه ، وصانعَهُ أَثرُ لَهُ ، فيتأَخَّرُ عنه ، والمؤخَّرُ عن المؤخّر عن الشيء مؤخّرٌ عن ذلك الشيء ضرورةً . وبالجملة : فاللازم في الدورِ أنْ يتقدَّمَ حصولُ الشيء على حصولِ نفسه بمرتبتين ، وأن يتأخَّرَ حصوله عن حصول نفسه بمرتبتين ، والتقدم والتأخر على ما ذُكِرَ متلازمان ، ولظهور برهان قدم الصانع وانتفاء الشبهة فيه .. لم يقل أحدٌ مِنَ العقلاء بحدوثِ صانع العالم
As for the refutation of circularity: I alluded to it in my statement in al-ʿAqīda: 'And in the second—meaning circularity—[it consists] in the fact that a single thing is prior to itself and posterior to it.' As for the necessity of its priority over itself: because its maker is an effect of it, so it must be prior to its maker; due to the necessity of the cause (muʾaththir) being prior to its effect (athar). But it is also an effect of its maker, so its maker must be prior to it for the same reason mentioned. So it follows that it is prior to itself by two ranks; because it is prior to its maker which is prior to itself, and that which is prior to that which is prior to something is necessarily prior to that something. And likewise it is necessary that it be posterior to itself by two ranks—and that is what I meant by my statement: 'and posterior to it'—because it is an effect of its maker, so it is posterior to it, and its maker is an effect of it, so it is posterior to it, and that which is posterior to that which is posterior to something is necessarily posterior to that something. In summary: what is entailed by circularity is that the existence of a thing is two ranks prior to its own existence and two ranks posterior to its own existence, and priority and posteriority as described are concomitant. And due to the clarity of the proof of the pre-eternity of the Creator and the elimination of doubt therein, none of the rational people have ever said that the Creator of the world is contingent (ḥādith).
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the logical impossibility of circular reasoning (dawr) in the proof of the Creator's eternity. The commentator first clarifies that circularity means a single thing being prior to itself and posterior to itself. He then explains the consequence: if A is the effect of B, and B is also the effect of A, then A must be prior to B (because the cause precedes its effect) and also posterior to B (because B is also its cause). This forces A to be two ranks prior to itself and two ranks posterior to itself, which is absurd. The argument shows that priority and posteriority are concomitant. Because the proof of the Creator's pre-eternity is clear and free from such circularity, no rational person has ever claimed the Creator is contingent.

Key Terms
دور (dawr)
قدم (qidam)
أثر (athar)
مؤثر (muʾaththir)
حادث (ḥādith)
صانع (ṣāniʿ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that circular reasoning (dawr) is a valid logical form in theological proofs, allowing reciprocal causation.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that circularity leads to an absurdity: a thing being both prior and posterior to itself by two ranks, which is impossible. Thus, circularity cannot be part of any valid proof.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator argue is the necessary consequence of circularity in proving the Creator's eternity?
A) The Creator must be contingent.
B) A single thing would be two ranks prior and two ranks posterior to itself.
C) Infinite regress of causes.
D) The proof becomes stronger.

Key Takeaway
Circularity leads to a logical contradiction (self-priority and self-posteriority), proving the Creator's eternity proof is sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself using a circular argument to justify your belief in Allah, without realizing its flaw? What does that reveal about the strength of your conviction?
?
Sanusi shows that circularity forces a thing to be prior to itself—an absurdity. In what areas of your faith might you be accepting premises that logically contradict each other?
?
The proof of the Creator's eternity is clear and free from doubt—but is your heart truly settled on that proof, or do you entertain subtle thoughts that imply Allah could be contingent? What would it take for you to fully internalize this certainty?

The Ash'ari Proof: Accidents Do Not Survive
Sanusi recounts the Ash'ari proof and its defense against the substance objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari proof that accidents cannot survive and how they respond to the objection that substances would also be impossible to cease.

Core Idea
Accidents cease instantly; substances endure only through constant renewal of accidents.

This passage from Sanusi presents a foundational Ash'ari argument: accidents have no duration and cease by their very existence. It also addresses a natural objection—if that is true, substances too would be impossible to cease—by explaining that substances persist only because God continuously creates accidents in them.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic and translation in one go. Notice this is not just a claim but a reasoning that includes a proof, an objection, and a response.
2
Understand the proof for accidents
The Imams argue: if accidents survived, their non-existence would be impossible (based on the earlier classification that enduring things need a cause to cease). But we observe that accidents do cease, so they never actually survived—they vanish by their very existence.
This is a proof by contradiction using the three rational judgments.
3
Examine the objection regarding substances
The same reasoning seems to apply to substances: substances endure, yet they can cease. If the rule were universal, their cessation would also be impossible. This forces a problem for the Ash'ari position.
This is a classic opponent's move called ilzam (compelling).
4
Learn the Ash'ari response
The Ash'aris answer: substances endure only because they are continuously supplied with accidents. When God wills to annihilate a substance, He stops creating accidents in it, and it ceases. Thus substances are not self-enduring; their endurance depends on accident generation.
This preserves the initial proof while explaining the difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنَّ بمثل هذا البرهان استدلَّ أئمَّةُ السنَّةِ رضي الله عنهم على استحالة بقاء الأعراض. قالوا : بل بنفسِ وجودِها تنعدمُ، ولا بقاء لها أصلاً، وسواء ما شُوهد فيهِ ذلكَ؛ كالحركاتِ والأصوات، أو لا؛ كالألوان والاعتقادات. قالوا : لأنَّها لو بقيتْ لاستحال عدمُها؛ لما ذُكر في التقسيم، فألزموا مثل ذلك في الجواهر مع أنَّها تبقى ويصح عدمُها، فأجابوا بأنَّ شرط بقائها إمدادها بالأعراض، فإذا أراد الله إعدامها قطع عنها خلق الأعراض
And know that with a similar proof the Imams of the Sunni community—may God be pleased with them—inferred the impossibility of the survival of accidents. They said: Rather, by their very existence they cease to exist, and they have no survival whatsoever, whether what is observed in that regard like movements and sounds, or not like colors and beliefs. They said: Because if they survived, their non-existence would be impossible, due to what was mentioned in the classification. Then they were compelled [to acknowledge] the same regarding substances, even though they endure and their non-existence is possible. Then they replied: The condition of their survival is that they be supplied with accidents; so if God wills to annihilate them, He cuts off from them the creation of accidents.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari proof for the impossibility of the survival (baqa') of accidents (a'rad). The Imams of the Sunni tradition used this proof to show that accidents do not endure; rather, they cease to exist by their very existence. This applies to all accidents, whether observable like movements and sounds, or non-observable like colors and beliefs (i'tiqadat). Their reasoning: If accidents survived, their non-existence would be impossible, based on the earlier classification (taqsim) that whatever endures cannot cease without a cause. Then the opponents forced them to apply the same reasoning to substances (jawahir), which do endure and yet their non-existence is possible. The Ash'aris responded: The condition for the survival of substances is that they are continuously supplied with accidents (i.e., God creates accidents in them). If God wills to annihilate a substance, He simply stops creating accidents in it, and it ceases to exist. So accidents themselves do not endure.

Key Terms
أعراض
بقاء
جواهر
إمداد
إعدام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Ash'ari doctrine makes all things transient, including substances.
Correction: The passage clarifies that substances do endure, but only because God continuously creates accidents within them. They are not self-enduring; their persistence depends on accident renewal.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari Imams, why would the survival of accidents lead to the impossibility of their non-existence?
A) Because accidents are eternal.
B) Because what survives cannot cease without a cause.
C) Because God creates them continually.
D) Because they are of the same genus as substances.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari proof establishes that accidents never survive, and substances continue only through God's constant creation of accidents in them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every accident in your body and mind ceases to exist the moment it appears, and God recreates it in the next, how does this affect your sense of identity? Are you the same 'you' from one moment to the next, or are you being remade by God each instant? What would it mean to live each moment as a new creation?
?
The Ash'ari argument says that even your beliefs (like your faith in God) are accidents that do not survive. They must be re-created by God every moment. When was the last time you felt your faith was something you owned versus a gift being continuously given? Would you treat your prayer, your thoughts, and your intentions differently if you knew they were being sustained by God right now, and could vanish if He withheld His grace?
?
You rely on substances like your body and the earth under your feet, which seem stable and independent. But the proof says they last only because God constantly supplies them with accidents. Consider something you take for granted, like your health or your family. Are you grateful for its continuation as a moment-by-moment act of God, or do you assume it will persist on its own? What would change if you woke up tomorrow aware that every stable thing is held in existence only by God's immediate will?
